    <li> This is an excellent shaver and impervious to water. After you use it just remove the foil shave head and wash it out under warm water. I keep it charged all the time by perching it on its charger, but I think you could go a couple of weeks between charges. I recall one reviewer saying he seldom charged it. This shaver has a sideburn and mustache trimmer that is a nice touch, just be careful when you get close to ears, nose or any body part because it can nick you. It can be elevated and retracted so make sure it is retracted until you&#x27;re ready to do trimming, and then keep it facing the opposite direction. It will keep your sideburns and mustache nicely sculpted. I like the look, feel, and ease of use of this shaver. It is an outstanding value and an excellent example of the latest shaving technology. You can even use it in the shower, or shave with cream of gel for a real smooth shave, although the lubrication somewhat defeats the cutting ability of the shaver. If you want a 5 o&#x27;clock shadow or stubble effect, shaving with cream is the way to go, and it makes for a relaxing, comforting shave. I&#x27;m really glad I discovered this shaver because it has saved me tons of $ on straight shaver blades. This shaver is strongly recommended; it delivers a smooth, clean shave and you will not be disappointed. One or two trips to the store to buy standard shaving blades will pay for this electric shaver. You can use it to shave body hair with decent results, but again, watch out for nicks with the retractable sideburn trimmer. This shaver is primarily designed for facial shaving.</li>
    <li> This product is effective.</li>

    <li> I&#x27;ve used electric shavers for about 40 years, which included Remington, Norelco, Panasonic, and Braun models.  My previous unit was also a Braun Series 3-340 shaver which held up well and was still working when I bought this current edition.  The reason I replaced the older unit was that I had dropped the shaver a few times and the sideburn trimmer had fallen apart as a result.  After 5 years of use, the shaver still shaved well and its&#x27; battery was still going strong.  This current model shaves my usual 3-day growth extremely well and is quieter than the previous unit.  I love how the blades/head hug the contours around my chin and jaw.  It is also easier to clean than my previous shaver, easier to handle, and comes with a head protector and a charging stand.  I&#x27;ve had this shaver for 3 weeks and so far have got around 8 shaves off the first charge which is impressive.  Time will tell how the unit holds up and how long the battery lasts but I am well pleased so far and would definitely buy one again.</li>
    <li> very good, I care much</li>
    <li> Replacing my old Braun after many years of service. The only brand I would ever buy. The new one shaves perfectly and needs recharging only every few weeks.</li>
    <li> I bought this to replace a ten year old electric that I used for a quick touch up between blade shaves.  I&#x27;ve used this one by itself for the last few weeks and I find that it does a reasonably good job.  The initial charge experience was a bit strange,because the green charge light does NOT stay lit throughout  the charging process.  I thought that there was a problem, but I contacted Braun Tech services and found out this was normal.  The initial charge took about seven or eight hours and I now charge it for about an hour once a week when the red low battery light turns on.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The razor itself shaves relatively close on face, cheek, and chin areas.  I find that I need to spend a lot of time with the trimmer on the neck and upper lip area.  I generally daily shave after my morning shower.  I do NOT use this in the shower though I think you can.  It cleans easily under running water and there is a small brush that helps.  It appears to be well sealed enough to use in the shower, but that&#x27;s just not my routine.  It&#x27;s not as close as a blade shave, but it does fine for me.  It has improved after a few weeks as my face has adapted to regular use of an electric again.&lt;br /&gt;There was a little redness and irritation on my neck for the first few days.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This is a reasonably priced alternative to the electrics with the fancy cleaning systems that can cost $200-$400.  I just can&#x27;t see spending that amount of money.  I also think that it&#x27;s crazy to spend $3 or $4 a week for disposable razors or blades.  This is a much more environmentally friendly and economical alternative in my opinion.  I look forward to years of regular use. though I may hang on to my blade razor to use once a week or so for a really close shave.  It should be noted that the manufacturer recommends changing the screen and cutter assembly about every eighteen months.  These seem to be fairly available on Amazon at a cost in the mid $20 range.</li>
    <li> Great close shave, long lasting battery, easy cleaning.&lt;br /&gt;First time user of non-Phillips shaver...happy I made the switch! Highly recommended.</li>

Yes, I was using it in the shower‚Äîwhich you are NOT supposed to do and I do NOT recommend you do.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;However, the precautions never say anything remotely close to &amp;#34;Never use this razor on a wet face!&amp;#34;‚Äîso let us proceed under the assumption that you are merely using the razor on a (your) wet face.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This model comes with a small tube of oil‚Äîdon&#x27;t lose it! In the manual, Braun advises that &amp;#34;if you regularly clean the shaver under water, then once a week apply a drop of light machine oil onto the long hair trimmer‚Ä¶and shaver Foil &amp; Cutter cassette.&amp;#34;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The instruction SHOULD go something like this: &amp;#34;If you like to completely wet your face before shaving, no problem, you will LOVE the awesomely close shave you&#x27;ll receive every time. ALL you have to remember is this: Every Single Time You Shave, you MUST MUST MUST remember to apply a drop of light machine oil (from the tube we so smartly have included with this model) onto a fingertip, and then carefully rub said oil into every single square millimeter of the long hair trimmer AND all the outward-facing metal parts of the shaver Foil &amp; Cutter cassette.&amp;#34;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;tl;dr: keep the Foil &amp; Cutter cassette oiled (oil it after every wet shave!), and you will love this razor</li>

That isn&#x27;t workable, except as a backup shaver.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I never had a Braun shaver before and figured it was time to try. This is the best shaver I&#x27;ve ever had. It&#x27;s easy to hold and use in all necessary positions.&lt;br/&gt;&lt;br /&gt;When I first got it, the charge would last about a week and half. It slowly dropped to a week. It turns out that the orange light for low battery gives a very generous warning time - a little too long. So the battery memory was shortening. I started letting the shaver run all the way down when the orange light came on. It seems like the braun shaver is heavier than it actually is.  The cut this provides is a pretty good shave, though it isn&#x27;t the best I&#x27;ve ever used. However, for the money paid, it does the job.    The shaver has a green light to show that there is a charge above 20% and a red light that flashes when the battery is low. Compared to other shaver, I tend to miss the LED percentages that give a more accurate idea of the charge status. However, most people this wouldn&#x27;t be an issue since you have it by the sink where you could plug it in with easy.    My biggest con of this shaver is that even with cleaning the hair out after ever 2 uses, the little hair trimmings seem to pour out when I use the razor. I&#x27;ll pick the razer off my desk and hair trimmings will fall out of it and it&#x27;s frankly quite annoying. It&#x27;s enough of a problem that I turn this new shaver into the backup of my old Panasonic shaver.    I give this a 4 star since 3 stars would probably be unfair as some of my complaints probably won&#x27;t be an issue with some people.    Pro  - good shaver  - battery life seems decently good    Con  - hair trimmings get everywhere  - a little heavier than some other razors    *If I&#x27;ve helped, let me know by hitting \\&quot;helpful\\&quot;*</li>

    <li> I bought the Braun 340S several weeks ago to replace my old Japanese-made Panasonic ES8066.  I bought that between six and nine years ago--not sure exactly.  The trimmer on it has gone bad and has pinched my skin several times causing large painful bumps when shaving my neck.  Otherwise it still works pretty well though the battery-life is about half what it was when new.  I have definitely gotten my money&#x27;s worth.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I don&#x27;t like the designs of the current Panasonics and they are no longer made in Japan.  So, I considered buying either this Braun or a Philips AT830 as a replacement.  The Philips costs about $15 more than what I was able to buy the Braun for in local stores (not Amazon).  I have never owned a Philips shaver.  I like their quietness but doubt one would shave as close as a foil shaver.  And, the head design would make it more difficult to shave precisely around my goatee.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I had a Braun shaver that was heavily marketed about ten years ago.  It was compact for travel and I initially liked the design.  But, it was not a good shaver.  It had a single cutter and was like trying to mow your entire lawn with a string trimmer.  There was just not enough cutting area.  The battery was wimpy.  It could be used while plugged in, so that helped negate the battery problem.  It only lasted a little over a year.  In spite of this, I decided to go with the Braun 340S given their 60-day trial period.  I have only used the shaver dry.  If I wanted to shave with the muss and fuss of gel or foam, I would just use a blade.  Mostly I use soap and water to do an extra good cleaning of the shaver.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Compared to my workhorse Panasonic, the Braun&#x27;s motor runs slower.  This gives the impression of being weaker.  However after a week of shaving one side of my face with the Braun and the other with the old Panasonic with a new foil my impression is the Braun may shave slightly closer.  Shaving time seems about the same.  I think the Braun gets neck hairs better.  But, you have to work at them.  I used to use the Panasonic&#x27;s trimmer for my neck before it quit working properly.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Replacing the Braun foil-cutter assembly is recommended every 18 months.  Philips recommends 12 months.  Panasonic recommends 12 months for the foil and 24 months for the cutter.  These costs definitely add to your total shaving costs, especially if you don&#x27;t search for a good deal.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I like the design of the Braun including the grip-ability of the rubber on the sides and the ridges on the front and back.  The curve of the body helps keep the head positioned properly against your skin.  The trimmer is straightforward and does a good job.  After several charges, I get up to 12 days of shaving on a charge.  Some reviews criticize the lack of a travel case for this model.  But the plastic head-cap offers good protection including blocking accidental pressing of the On Button.  If you don&#x27;t have a case, you could just stuff it in one of your clean socks during travel.  It fits well in the velvet case I still have from my old Panasonic so, for me, there is no issue.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;In summary, I rate the Braun 340S as 4-stars.  It is as good as, but not superior to, anything I have used.  Reviews lead me to believe other shavers may be superior, e.g., the Braun Series 7.  But, for 2.5x the price of this shaver I doubt they are worth it.  A blade shaves closer but for me not enough so to be worth the fuss of lathering up other than for special occasions.</li>

I don&#x27;t but you can, probably ladies would be interested in that.  Its much better than the braun I had 30 years ago, but not much has changed.  I guess when its not broken, braun isn&#x27;t going to fix it.  That is impressive.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;UPDATE 9/2014:  OK, I have been using this for several months now, and thought I would update.  First off, the good:&lt;br /&gt;1- Shaves good --IF CLEAN.&lt;br /&gt;2- Great battery life, (1 week plus)&lt;br /&gt;3- light weight&lt;br /&gt;4- nice charger stand&lt;br /&gt;5- easy to disassemble and clean&lt;br /&gt;6 trimmer works great&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;THE BAD:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If this is not cleaned (rinsed out with blade off), every 2 days or so, you will notice the quality of the shave declines rapidly.  It will get to the point it almost does nothing.  So its imperative you keep this cleaned out.  The other issue I have is that the trimmer is very awkward and kind of ungainly.  Its good for trimming side burns, but its almost worthless for trimming around ears or neck because of the size and angles that the trimmer is mounted.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;All in all for under 60$ I am very impressed and very happy.  Initially I was going to remove a star, but as I think about it, my big issue is that I need to clean it?  I mean that is a given, and how can I deduct for that.  I point it out so that you are aware of it and you keep yours cleaned vs thinking its not working.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I hope this is helpful.</li>

    <li> It&#x27;s pretty unreasonable to expect any electric razor to give a close shave in a pass or two; manufacturers can&#x27;t possibly know how fast a &amp;#34;pass&amp;#34; will be, or at what angle whiskers are growing. One always has to do many passes over cheek or neck from different angles to get a very smooth result. That&#x27;s life.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;ve been a Panasonic user for 11 years. Have always gotten a very close shave. First one lasted 3 years. Last one has lasted 8 years...and without changing any foils or blades! (And my beard is no softer than anyone&#x27;s.) So Panasonic has been good value for me.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;However, Panasonic has gotten incredibly expensive, and they all have &amp;#34;arc&amp;#34; shapes which is opposite what a face needs...and they went down the &amp;#34;ultra high rpms&amp;#34; road, which I believe is wasted wear and tear...not to mention loud. 13,000 new whiskers can&#x27;t possibly find themselves into the same foil hole in a second&#x27;s time. At most a dozen, and likely far less. So a couple hundred rpm ought to be more than enough.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;That was part of my theory when I went looking for alternatives to the Panasonic price tag. I&#x27;ve tried rotary models (Norelco) which work quietly but don&#x27;t give nearly as close a shave (although they do the job enough to go to work and such). And I&#x27;ve tried a Remington foil model, but found that Remington gets their money not up front but on foil replacements--the foil warps and then tears/breaks after 3 months.  Not good.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So this time I tried Braun. Didn&#x27;t need any fancy clean-and-lube features (skin has a little oil on it anyway). This Braun 340s is very nice. Much quieter than the Panasonic, slower speed, low-frequency rumble...but the shave is just as good. Could even be superior, although I&#x27;m comparing a new Braun to an 8-year-old Panasonic. Still, it takes me no longer to shave than it ever did. Braun says their foils have hole openings that aren&#x27;t uniformly round, and that probably helps the result.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;An admittedly bizarre-sounding side benefit which no one ever mentions is that the low rumble vibration of the Braun is low enough frequency that your face can feel it. It&#x27;s a bit like a face muscle massage (compared to the Panasonic). Sounds ridiculous? Yeah, well, the face has a lotta muscles, believe it or not; keeping them &amp;#34;fit&amp;#34; and flexible has been shown to keep a face from sagging and making a guy look like a 100-year-old basset hound before he&#x27;s all that old. If I care enough to want to shave, I care enough to not have jowls before my time. The Braun feels good on the muscles. (I don&#x27;t know, maybe I need it because I grimace too much.) For what it&#x27;s worth....&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This Braun shaver has a solid, durable feel to it. Has a small charging stand that&#x27;s all you need. Seems to charge quickly. The side-burns/moustache trimmer is superior to the one on my Panasonic. It&#x27;s just as easy to dump whiskers out of the Braun. And (sorry to be so graphic, but) the whisker dust is a lot less fine, courtesy once again of the lower frequency. You can see the diff very easily.  And there&#x27;s a lot more of it when it&#x27;s dumped out--which means my Panasonic was chopping whiskers into a dust so fine it was losing that dust out the foil holes...onto the bathroom counter, my shirt, etc. I never knew it until now.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Bottom line, I like the Braun a lot.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Can&#x27;t speak about how long the battery, foils or blade will last, as I&#x27;ve only had it about a month. Feels durable. Since you can also get a better deal with a Braun,  I expect this 340s to give me equal (maybe superior) value to the Panasonic models I&#x27;ve used before.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If my Panasonic&#x27;s battery was still lasting through a full shave every day (which it wasn&#x27;t), I wouldn&#x27;t have shopped for a Braun. But if, like me, it&#x27;s time for you to consider a new razor, I&#x27;d recommend this Braun 340s. Good machine.</li>

    <li> My Norelco of, oh, let&#x27;s say 14 years because who can tell, finally started to go on me and I decided it was time to upgrade, after enveloping myself in the bevy of reviews and opinions in this apparently gargantuan electric shaving community it became clear a foil shaver would resolve my irritation issues - or so I was told. This shaver is essentially the same as 380S-4 (which has an additional switch for closer shaves under nose, neck etc., comes with a pleather pouch and has 3 indicators for battery charge vs. two on 340S-4). Panasonic was never good near the neck area and this Braun does so much better than Panasonic. Probably because Braun has a narrower head (3 blades) vs. the wider head of Panasonic (4 blades). Perfect scenario were less is more! It takes about 5-6 minutes for a very close shave, which also I think is lesser than what Panasonic used to take.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;There is a trimmer which can be used for sideburns or moustaches but I don&#x27;t like the design and location of where it is (its on the back with a sliding mechanism) and I usually use a disposable razor for that. This is a major convenience for me since I was used to just putting the Panasonic back in to the cleaner/charger. The cleaners are mostly a waste and running the shaver in water with liquid soap is more than enough. There is also a plastic head cover which protects the head while traveling, but I wish it case with a case.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;ve only had it for two weeks so I can&#x27;t comment on the durability.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cons -&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Build quality is not the same as Panasonic (well its cheaper). The power switch feels flimsy and I have a feeling it won&#x27;t last very long. Especially if you do wet shave and clean your shaver every few strokes in running water.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall 5 stars. Just for that super close, soft and smooth shave!     <li> Some things never change! Perelli makes the best tires, Sony makes the best TVs, Leica makes the best cameras.  And Braun makes the best shavers, offering the best construction and design, sharpest blades, the strongest motors, the greatest longevity, and the closest shave in the business!&lt;br /&gt;Specifics, you want? Okay!&lt;br /&gt;The first thing you notice upon opening the &#x27;tamper proof&#x27; packaging is the robust construction and materials used for this shaver. It feels &#x27;solid&#x27;, like it could easily survive several drops to a tile bathroom fall without so much as a scratch.  If you&#x27;re REALLY observant, you&#x27;ll see why. While constructed largely of plastic and other synthetics, they&#x27;re the same industrial grade materials used in your Nikon and Canon DSLR bodies and lens housings. Even the molded handle is the same tough, &#x27;grippy&#x27; rubberlike compound as the handgrips of your Nikon D7100, and exhibited similarly excellent ergonomics. While I haven&#x27;t subjected the shaver to any MIL-STD-810J shock tests...nor do I plan to...these are TOUGH materials, designed to last! My &#x27;old&#x27; Braun shaver &#x27;resigned&#x27; after 15 years of loyal, unwavering service. How&#x27;s that for &#x27;product longevity&#x27;!  The entire shaver housing, including the encapsulated power switch, side trimmer, and motor to cutter head coupling  are fully sealed and waterproof. This shaver is intended for both wet and dry shaving. I&#x27;ve tried it in both dry and in the shower (using only Ivory handsoap for &#x27;shaving creme&#x27;) and performance is exemplary however you prefer to shave; \\&quot;baby&#x27;s butt smooth\\&quot;...every time! All the more impressive given that my Nixon-esque beard is more like high-carbon steel wire, case hardened to Rockwell C-70, than actual human hair.  The powerful motor in this instrument cut through my facial flora more like a laser than a razor. By contrast, Panasonic and Remington best just &#x27;couldn&#x27;t cut it&#x27;, their motors sounding anemic; as if they might \\&quot;stall under load\\&quot; at any moment, and worse, after 15 minutesuse, they still left me in need of a shave! The Braun, as I said, left my face perfectly clean and smooth, without ANY burning or irritation.&lt;br /&gt;In conclusion, I am delighted to confer upon the Braun Series 3, 340S-4 shaver my very highest recommendation. When used dry it&#x27;s about as good as sandpaper and sharp rocks and there is never a point where I say &amp;#34;Yes, my face is now nice and clean shaven.&amp;#34;. The reason it has so much trouble shaving necks, as many other reviewers have noted, seems to be a core engineering problem. The shaving foils that do the cutting are spaced too far away from each other and have too much plastic bezel surrounding them, which means on any curved surface it has a great deal of trouble making contact with both at the same time. You might as well be shaving with a $20 single foil razor, which coincidentally is about the quality of shave you&#x27;re getting from the 340S-4.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;It gets 1 star for being water proof and for being easy to clean under the sink. I thought of this as a great alternative, I had also heard of Brauns superior build quality. I had grown some serious stubble (+4 days) and put it to the test. It takes quite a bit longer than a normal razor, but the outcome is better, at least for me I got no irritation, and no bumps because I used it with a cooling shaving cream. Also with this, unlike normal razors you go against the grain, and if you have any tight corners in your face it will miss those and you have to pass them again, hence why it probably takes slightly longer when you first use it. However it could be a time saver, if you use it in the shower. It feels very nice in the hand, it&#x27;s very lightweight, and I feel it could last much more than 2-3 years. It also comes with a cleaning brush and machine oil for it. A slight recommendation would be up the motors power a bit, I feel it wouldn&#x27;t have missed stubble if it had a bit more power too it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Shipping: The shipping for this in the Philadelphia area SUCKED!! Thankfully I had contacted amazon and they refunded the entire cost of shipping and shipping tax for me.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Pros:&lt;br /&gt;Lightweight&lt;br /&gt;Can be used in the shower&lt;br /&gt;Nice Build Quality&lt;br /&gt;If you&#x27;ve used disposable razors you&#x27;re entire life&lt;br /&gt;Almost comparable shave to razors&lt;br /&gt;NO CUTS!!&lt;br /&gt;Built in trimmer can do sideburns really well&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cons:&lt;br /&gt;Needs a tad bit more power so it can cut hair a bit quicker&lt;br /&gt;You have to add machine oil to the foils/blades if you wash them all the time (at least once a week if under continuous washing)?     <li> This Braun 340S-4 is so much better than my previous Braun shaver.  The older version (5776) was flimsier. Compared with the older 5776, the construction of the 340S-4 is superior in every way.  The Cutter-Foil Cartridge is solidly designed albeit expensive.  The 5776&#x27;s Cartridge was a mess and the trimmer kept disconnecting from the main body of the shaver.  I am glad that Braun fixed this in the 340S-4 model.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I shave every day, and I shave my full head, not just my face.  I find this Braun 340S-4 to be very comfortable, close shaving, well made and non-irritating.  I have nothing to say against this shaver, but it IS on the pricy side.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I do have to rework some areas of my head and face to get the shave that I want, but I so far have not seen any shaver that did better.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I get three shaves from a single charge which is better than the 5776 did, but I miss the fact that the 5776 allowed me to shave while charging, which the newer 340S-4 does not (it will not charge &amp; shave at the same time).  Beware, if you sometimes fail to charge your shaver, you may get half a shave.  There is a red warning light though, and you probably have a full shave left even when it comes on, but do not ignore it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The engineering of the 340S-4 seems well thought out and built to last, but only time will tell.  I got about a year and a half to two years of life from my previous Braun shavers.  The feature that spells certain death for the Braun shavers has been the hinge-joint which allows the shaver head to swivel as you perform you shave.  It eventually breaks rendering the shaver useless.  This doubtful advantage has been thankfully removed in the 340S-4. From past experience, I have noticed that recharge life will gradually shorten over time until the shaver becomes next to useless as well, unless you can recharge while shaving. This is normal for any rechargeable battery, but there is no way to replace this battery in the Braun shavers, so this may be the new Achilles heal of the 340S-4.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I do not miss the black carry case of the older shavers because the carry case was poorly designed anyway and would break into two pieces at the flimsy hinge.  Also the case would soon warp so that the two halves did not properly align after only a few months of use.  This 340S-4 does not have a carry case at all but rather a plastic head cover which is one piece and pretty much gets the job of protection done.</li>

    <li> I have used an electric shaver for more than twenty years.  And, over the years, I have acquired several shavers, each of which had its strong points as well as its weaker ones.  For example, Hitachi makes shavers with roller blades much like the manual push lawnmowers, and Norelco makes the rotary shavers.  The Hitachi is great for one-day growths, but doesn&#x27;t do all that well with longer hairs.  The Norelco (Philips), on the other hand, does a great job with longer hairs, but for me, at least, is not the greatest with a one-day growth.  And, finally, my favorite was a Grundig shaver, but the sliding switch just broke, and new ones are no longer available in the U.S.A., just in Europe.  So, I am always so grateful to other reviewers on Amazon, because I can often get a good idea from them before ordering.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;That was the case with this Braun shaver (also because I have had good service from assorted Braun kitchen gadgets).  This shaver gets the longer and the shorter facial and neck hairs equally well.  The trimmer cuts even longer hairs that crop up low on my neck without irritating the skin.  I opted for the model that works in the shower, and I have used it on my wet face just after the shower for a very close shave.  The rubber non-slip skin that encloses the shaver is a huge plus.  All-in-all, this is as perfect a shaver as I could hope for. I recommend this purchase.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Footnote: Be sure to order the Braun 32b Series 3 Combi Replacement Pack.  It has the randomly spaced holes, whereas the shaver comes with regularly spaced holes.  I expect that when I have to replace the one-piece head with the Braun 32b Series 3 Combi Replacement Pack, I will get as good or better shave.</li>

    <li> I purchased this model shaver from Wallyworld, but wanted to share my quick down and dirty review here, as Amazon is where I gathered my initial info while standing in the aisle.  At the time I didnt have Prime, and I needed it ASAP rather than a few days away.  So far, I&#x27;ve owned it 8 months.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;First off, this is my first real electric.  I&#x27;ve had other generic travel foil shavers, but nothing of substantial sturdiness.  This is one sturdy unit.  It has survived several drops in the shower without any issue.  You cant even visually tell its fallen to the floor.  Still hums like day one.  All well and good.  I will say, like most other reviewers, it does take several passes to get a smooth cut, especially on the neck.  I&#x27;ve found it easiest to hold the razor so its foils are up and down (perpendicular to the floor), tilt my head back, and make good horizontal swipes like I am trying to slice my own neck.  That motion gets the best results with me.  It might work with you too.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Right, continuing the review...battery life is sweet.  I charge it once a week, and shave about 7 minutes a day, 6 days a week...sometimes wet in the shower, or dry before I get in....depending on the previous day&#x27;s growth.  I&#x27;d say it does much better dry than wet, but the unit it at home in either environment.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The ugly is the head replacement.  You read in the manuals to replace the cutting head every 18 months.  I must have some radioactive diamond coated whiskers on my face, because my head began to have issues keeping up at month #6.  I&#x27;ve dealt with it, and attempted to clean and oil the thing to no avail for the last two months.  I broke down and spent the $27 for a new head today, and it went to down like it was day one all over again...which is what prompted me to write this review.  Having to spend $27 every six months for a new foil sucks, especially when Braun says it should last 18 months, but the time savings of electric vs manual kind of evens the score.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall, I am satisfied with the purchase.  I am ecstatic about the price compared to comparable brands.  I am happy with the build quality.  I am happy with the battery life.  I am satisfied with the cut (even the annoying areas on my neck that never seem to be cut on the first or fifth swipe).  I am neutral on the cutting head&#x27;s life.  I dislike the cost of new heads at roughly $27.  The downsides are why I give the 4 star score instead of 5.</li>

But really, I&#x27;ve never had any part on any other electric shaver I&#x27;ve owned (Norelco, Remington, or Panasonic) break.  I have to re-rate this shaver from five stars to four stars. It does an OK job when you are in a hurry and can do a great job if you take your time (3-5 minutes).  The pop-up trimmer is excellent too.  I am sorry I didn&#x27;t get one of these years ago.  This razor can also be used with shaving cream in the shower...have not tried this yet but expect it would be great too.  The charge seems to last a couple of weeks and fully recharges in an hour.  Also, in 18 months, you can replace the cutter for about $20 and essentially have a new razor. Clean up after a shave couldn&#x27;t be easier: the razor is a snap to clean.&lt;br /&gt;Ergonomically, the razor feels sure and steady in the hand and is very attractive and obviously well made.  I did a lot of research on Amazon and this razor seemed to have the best price vs. performance ratio of all that I looked at.  I don&#x27;t see how anyone could make a mistake with this purchase unless they have an exceptionally heavy beard to contend with.</li>

    <li> I am trying to like this shaver. I received it as a gift after my 7000 series would no longer hold a charge. This one is quieter and lighter than my old one, but doesn&#x27;t look or feel near as solid (but it is a much cheaper shaver.) I have used the shaver for over 6 months. The first month of shaving gave a really nice shave, but since then it doesn&#x27;t seem to be as close a shave and feels more abrasive. I would say that the cutter should be replaced every 3 or 4 months. I&#x27;ve been twice painfully bitten by this shaver - the first time when I accidentally switched it off while shaving and it yanked a whisker out, the other time by the narrow joint between the foil and the cutter assembly. The major deficiencies I see with this shaver are: 1) The on/off button is right where your thumb wants to be when holding it, making it very easy to accidentally turn it off while shaving. My older 7000 series had a switch that had to be pressed and then slid upward and so it was practically impossible to turn it off by accident. 2) The plastic cover fits over the cutters and the switch, however it pops off very easily. Rarely will I find it in place even when just sitting in my drawer. The cover won&#x27;t keep the switch from being pressed. I had this shaver in my luggage during a short trip, only to find that the press of the clothes pressed the switch on even with the cover on it. When I got to my destination, the shaver had clearly been turned on, running down the battery, 3) The cutter assembly has a narrow space between the metal foil and the plastic structure around it. It is very easy for a whisker to be caught in that and the whisker will be yanked out - very painful!  In my opinion this shaver is okay for its price, but not near the quality of the older (and more expensive) Braun shavers. For its price, it&#x27;s good but you have to be willing to accept the poorly placed on/off button and beware that the cutter could painfully snag a whisker. It might be that the new high-end Brauns are as good as my old one was and I might try a new series 7 if I get bit by this one again.</li>

    <li> This review is specifically for the Braun 3Series 340S-4 Wet &amp; Dry Shaver.  I&#x27;m a long time Braun fan, and have used the Braun 6820 foil shaver for years. My original order was mysteriously returned before it even arrived, so I contacted Amazon - kudo&#x27;s to Amazon customer service who helped me to get another on order immediately and even waived the next-day shipping.&lt;br /&gt;The new shaver arrived and I immediately charged it up. I like the charger base, very convenient to stand the razor on and charge when not in use. The razor is light and comfortable to hold, but noticeably bulkier than the old model. This one won&#x27;t fit in my travel kit, and it did not come with a travel case. It did come with a plastic shield to protect the foil and keep the power button from being depressed in a suitcase. The first thing I noticed when using the razor however is that the dual-foil design has the shorter foils spaced further apart with the long-hair cutter between. The model I formerly used has longer, narrower foils and is easier to maneuver over the face. A dry-shave with this razor is noticeably not as close as my previous razor. It does a somewhat better job when my beard is longer (1.5-2 days growth) than when trying to dry-shave a shorter 5:00 shadow. I don&#x27;t normally use any electric-shave pre-shaving product, perhaps that would help.  This morning I tried it in the shower for the first time as a wet shaver. I quickly discovered that it is useless without some lubricant (I soaped my face with  bar soap). Again, it did a passable job, but still not the closeness I am accustomed to.     <li> I have owned countless Panasonic wet/dry shavers over the past 15 years and replaced my last busted Panasonic with this Braun shaver.  My review compares this Braun to the Panasonic shavers I&#x27;ve had.  I have owned regular Panasonic shavers as well as the ones with the &amp;#34;Linear&amp;#34; motor.  I&#x27;ve had the Braun for about 2 months now.  I have a pretty thick beard that&#x27;s still somewhat visible after any type of shave (electric or razor) and I must shave everyday.  Regular razors tear up my skin and cause breakouts, so I have to use an electric shaver.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Wet shave (while in shower):&lt;br /&gt;The Braun is so much quieter than any Panasonic shaver I&#x27;ve owned.  The Braun does a nice job with a little bit of foam shaving cream (I don&#x27;t recommend shaving gels since they are too thick).  My shave comes out very close and it only takes about 2-3 minutes.  The only part of my face that doesn&#x27;t come out well is my neck.  I usually have to do some touch-ups on my neck after I get out of the shower.  I would say the Braun shaves slightly better than Panasonic and a few minutes faster.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Dry shave:&lt;br /&gt;Dry shaving performance is not acceptable if I was going into work the same day.  It simply doesn&#x27;t shave close enough for my boss&#x27; liking.  But it&#x27;s close enough for weekends and days off.  Dry shaving is super quick.  But I would say the Panasonic shavers work better for dry shaving.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Other random thoughts:&lt;br /&gt;The Braun seems well made and is a bit bigger than the Panasonic shavers.  It charges in an hour using a NiCd battery and I can get about 8-9 days out of a single charge (I expect to charge the unit more often as the battery ages).  The trimmer works fine. It also comes with an international voltage charger and a protective cap for the blades to be used when travelling.  Braun&#x27;s marketing material claims this shaver will last 7 years, but I really doubt it!  This model of Braun is one of the few Brauns that can be used in the shower- most Brauns are dry shave only.  So pay attention to the specs!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall, I like this shaver better than Panasonic shavers.  The problem I have with Panasonic shavers is that the rubber seals break after about 1-1.5 years.  When the seals break, water gets in the unit causing the display to malfunction and for the unit to not charge. Panasonic offers a 2 year warranty on most shavers and I sent a couple of shavers in to be serviced, but the seal ALWAYS breaks again a few months later.  Then when you get close to the end of the 2 year warranty, the dilemma is &amp;#34;Do I send it in to be serviced again and replace the blades and foil  (which are about forty to fifty bucks) and risk it breaking again, or do I buy a new shaver for about ten bucks more?&amp;#34;  I always chose to buy a new shaver.  (Of course if you use the Panasonic for dry shaving only the seals should be ok for years.)  The other problem with Panasonic shavers is the &amp;#34;Linear&amp;#34; motor, which uses a lithium ion battery and is much more powerful than their standard shavers which use NiCd batteries.  The Linear motor is so powerful that the vibration loosens up the shaver&#x27;s case and blade cartridge in a few months and causes the unit to rattle VERY loud when beng used.  Interestingly, I found no difference between the shave quality of Panasonic&#x27;s  Linear or standard shavers, but the Linear is a faster shave.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Hope this helps.</li>

    <li> I&#x27;ve been a loyal Braun user for 30+ years and was always satisfied with their entry-level models.  This year, I treated myself to a Braun 720 to see what I&#x27;ve been missing.  After using it for 6 months, I bought a Braun 340s and am much happier with that model.  Here&#x27;s why:  Shaving:  I think Braun optimized the 720 for comfort, but went too far.  The shaver head is sprung so soft that it really doesn&#x27;t do a good job of getting the blades next to your skin to cut your beard.  I had to go over and over my face to get a complete shave and was still left with stubble that I could feel no matter how long I shaved or which angle I used.  The shaver head in the 340s is sprung much firmer.  The result is fewer passes, less time shaving and a noticeably closer and smoother shave.  Trimmer:  The trimmer on the 720 is just plain terrible.  It folds out from the side of the body at an odd angle, sticks out a couple of wobbly inches and has a curved blade (like a letter &amp;#34;D&amp;#34;, with the curve sticking out).  What part of a man&#x27;s face curves inward in a way that will fit that shape?  Heads are round, not shaped like an hourglass!  The curve means that only the middle half-inch of the trimmer does anything and the weird angle and length mean that it is hard to position to get a clean, straight trim.  The trimmer on the 340s, on the other hand, is straight so the whole width can be used and it slides straight up from the side of the body to be close and level with the shaver head, so you know exactly how the trimmer blade is aligned without even looking at it.  The result is straight, even sideburns with one pass.  Longer hair:  I have a short goatee and the 720 shaver head was always snagging my beard (ouch!) when shaving up to the edge of it.  I don&#x27;t have this problem with the 340s.  3 speeds v. 1 speed:  The 3 speeds on the 720 didn&#x27;t have any noticeable effect other than to change the sound of the shaver.  The single speed on the 340s works just fine.  So, for me, the 340s is the better shaver on performance and ease of use.  The cost saving compared to the 7 Series is just icing on the cake.</li>
